<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Traditional_heralds">Traditional heralds</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nowruz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Traditional heralds">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Amu_Nowruz_and_Haji_Firuz">Amu Nowruz and Haji Firuz</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nowruz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Amu Nowruz and Haji Firuz">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Amu_Nowruz" title="Amu Nowruz">Amu Nowruz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hajji_Firuz" title="Hajji Firuz">Hajji Firuz</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Amu_Nowruz.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Amu_Nowruz.jpg/170px-Amu_Nowruz.jpg" width="170" height="201" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Amu_Nowruz.jpg/255px-Amu_Nowruz.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Amu_Nowruz.jpg/340px-Amu_Nowruz.jpg 2x" data-file-width="638" data-file-height="756" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Amu_Nowruz.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Amu_Nowruz" title="Amu Nowruz">Amu Nowruz</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Haji_Firuz_on_the_road.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Haji_Firuz_on_the_road.jpg/220px-Haji_Firuz_on_the_road.jpg" width="220" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Haji_Firuz_on_the_road.jpg/330px-Haji_Firuz_on_the_road.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Haji_Firuz_on_the_road.jpg/440px-Haji_Firuz_on_the_road.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3920" data-file-height="2872" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Haji_Firuz_on_the_road.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Hajji_Firuz" title="Hajji Firuz">Haji Firuz</a> performers on a road to <a href="/wiki/Tehran" title="Tehran">Tehran</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In Iran, the traditional heralds of the festival of Nowruz are <a href="/wiki/Amu_Nowruz" title="Amu Nowruz">Amu Nowruz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hajji_Firuz" title="Hajji Firuz">Haji Firuz</a>, who appear annually in the streets to celebrate the New Year.</p>
<p>Amu Nowruz brings children gifts, much like his <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christian</a> counterpart <a href="/wiki/Santa_Claus" title="Santa Claus">Santa Claus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> He is the husband of <a href="/wiki/Nane_Sarma" title="Nane Sarma">Nane Sarma</a>, with whom he shares a traditional love story in which they can meet each other only once a year.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> He is characterized as an elderly silver-haired man who puts on a felt hat, and has a walking stick, a long cloak of blue canvas, a sash, a pair of thin-soled <a href="/wiki/Giveh" title="Giveh">giveh</a>, and a pair of linen trousers.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup></p>
<p>Haji Firuz, a blackface character clad in bright red clothes and a felt hat, is the companion of Amu Nowruz. He dances through the streets while singing and playing a tambourine. In the traditional songs, he introduces himself as a serf trying to cheer people who he refers to as his lords. As a blackface serf, it is a controversial character, seen as symbolically racist.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> Therefore, half of his face is sometimes painted white in order to prevent the criticisms.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Kampirak">Kampirak</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nowruz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Kampirak">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In the folklore of Afghanistan, Kampirak and his retinue pass village by village distributing gathered charities among people. He is an old bearded man wearing colorful clothes with a long hat and rosary who symbolizes beneficence and the power of nature yielding the forces of winter. The tradition is observed in central provinces, specially <a href="/wiki/Bamyan_Province" title="Bamyan Province">Bamyan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Daykundi_Province" title="Daykundi Province">Daykundi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Visiting_one_another">Visiting one another</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nowruz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Visiting one another">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>During the Nowruz holidays, people are expected to visit one another (mostly limited to families, friends and neighbors) in the form of short house visits, which are usually reciprocated. Typically, the youth will visit the elders first, and the elders return their visit later.</p>
<p>In Iran, the visits naturally have to be relatively short, otherwise one will not be able to visit everybody on the list. A typical visit is lesser than 30 minutes, where you often run into other visiting relatives and friends who happen to be paying a visit to the same house at that time.</p>
<p>Because of the house visits, you make sure you have a sufficient supply of pastry, cookies, fresh and dried fruits and mixed nuts on hand, as you typically serve your visitors with these items with tea and other beverages. Many Iranians will throw large Nowruz parties in a central location as a way of dealing with the long distances between groups of friends and family.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sizdebedar">Sizdebedar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nowruz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Sizdebedar">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sizdah_Be-dar" title="Sizdah Be-dar">Sizdebedar</a></div>
<p>In Iran, the Nowruz holidays last thirteen days. On the thirteenth day of the New Year, Iranians leave their houses to join nature and <a href="/wiki/Picnic" title="Picnic">picnic outdoors</a>, as part of the <a href="/wiki/Sizdah_Be-dar" title="Sizdah Be-dar">Sizdebedar</a> ceremony.</p>
<p>On the day of Sizdebedar, the greenery grown for the <a href="/wiki/Haft_Seen" class="mw-redirect" title="Haft Seen">Haft Seen</a> setting is thrown away, particularly into a running water. It is also customary for young single people, especially young girls, to tie the leaves of the greenery before discarding it, expressing a wish to find a partner.</p>
<p>Another custom associated with Sizdebedar is <i>Lie of the Thirteen</i>, which is the process of lying to someone and making them believe it.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> It has been directly borrowed from <a href="/wiki/April_Fools%27_Day" title="April Fools' Day">April Fools' Day</a>, and has become in vogue in Iran due to its coincidence with the day of the celebration of Sizdebedar.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nowruz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Baklava_-_Turkish_special,_80-ply.JPEG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Baklava_-_Turkish_special%2C_80-ply.JPEG/170px-Baklava_-_Turkish_special%2C_80-ply.JPEG" width="170" height="113" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Baklava_-_Turkish_special%2C_80-ply.JPEG/255px-Baklava_-_Turkish_special%2C_80-ply.JPEG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Baklava_-_Turkish_special%2C_80-ply.JPEG/340px-Baklava_-_Turkish_special%2C_80-ply.JPEG 2x" data-file-width="1542" data-file-height="1024" /></a>

</div>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Desserts_and_snacks">Desserts and snacks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nowruz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Desserts and snacks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul>
<li>Ajil (<a href="/wiki/Kurds" title="Kurds">Kurds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Persian_people" title="Persian people">Persians</a>): <a href="/wiki/Trail_mix" title="Trail mix">Trail mix</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Baklava" title="Baklava">Baklava</a> (<a href="/wiki/Azerbaijanis" title="Azerbaijanis">Azerbaijanis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Persian_people" title="Persian people">Persians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkish_people" title="Turkish people">Turks</a>): A flaky pastry filled with walnuts, almonds or pistachios, and flavored with rosewater</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Falooda" title="Falooda">Falooda</a> dessert (<a href="/wiki/Parsi" title="Parsi">Parsis</a>): A sweet milk drink made from vermicelli and flavored with rose essence</li>
<li>Lagan-nu-custard dessert (<a href="/wiki/Parsi" title="Parsi">Parsis</a>): A type of <a href="/wiki/Cr%C3%A8me_caramel" title="Crème caramel">caramel custard</a>.</li>
<li>Nan berenji (<a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iranians</a>): Cookies made from <a href="/wiki/Rice_flour" title="Rice flour">rice flour</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Noghl" title="Noghl">Noql</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pashtuns" title="Pashtuns">Pashtuns</a>, <a href="/wiki/Persian_people" title="Persian people">Persians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tajiks" title="Tajiks">Tajiks</a>): Sugar-coated almonds</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Samanu" title="Samanu">Samanu</a> (<a href="/wiki/Azerbaijanis" title="Azerbaijanis">Azerbaijanis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kurds" title="Kurds">Kurds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Persian_people" title="Persian people">Persians</a>): Sprouted wheat pudding</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Shekerbura" title="Shekerbura">Shekerbura</a> (<a href="/wiki/Azerbaijanis" title="Azerbaijanis">Azerbaijanis</a>): Azerbaijani sweet pastries</li>
<li>Shorgoghal (<a href="/wiki/Azerbaijanis" title="Azerbaijanis">Azerbaijanis</a>): Flaky bread with a spice filling</li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Dishes">Dishes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nowruz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Dishes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ash_reshteh" title="Ash reshteh">Ash e reshte</a> (<a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iranians</a>): A noodle soup traditionally served on the first day of Nowruz.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup></li>
<li>Chicken farcha (<a href="/wiki/Parsi" title="Parsi">Parsis</a>): A typical Parsi dish of fried chicken.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dolma" title="Dolma">Dolma</a> (<a href="/wiki/Azerbaijanis" title="Azerbaijanis">Azerbaijanis</a>): A traditional dish of Azeri people, cooked just before the New Year. It includes vegetables, meat and rice which have been cooked, then rolled in grape leaves and cooked again.</li>
<li>Fried fish and jelabi (<a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghans</a>): The most often meal of the Nauruz picnics in Afghanistan.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kuku_(food)" title="Kuku (food)">Kuku sabzi</a> (<a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iranians</a>): Herbs and vegetable <a href="/wiki/Souffl%C3%A9" title="Soufflé">soufflé</a>, traditionally served for dinner on New Year's. It is a light and fluffy omelet made with parsley, dill herb, coriander greens (cilantro), <a href="/wiki/Spinach" title="Spinach">spinach</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spring_onion" class="mw-redirect" title="Spring onion">spring onion</a> leaves and chives, mixed with eggs and <a href="/wiki/Walnut" title="Walnut">walnuts</a>.</li>
<li>Kulcha-e Nauruz (<a href="/wiki/Pashtuns" title="Pashtuns">Pashtuns</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tajiks" title="Tajiks">Tajiks</a>): Afghan rice cookies which are only baked for Nauruz.</li>
<li>Nawrz koje (<a href="/wiki/Kazakhs" title="Kazakhs">Kazakhs</a>): A traditional New Year's Day dish of the Kazakh people, which includes water, meat, salt, flour, grain and milk.</li>
<li>Reshte polow (<a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iranians</a>): Rice cooked with noodles.</li>
<li>Sabzi chalaw (<a href="/wiki/Pashtuns" title="Pashtuns">Pashtuns</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tajiks" title="Tajiks">Tajiks</a>): A dish made from rice and <a href="/wiki/Spinach" title="Spinach">spinach</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sabzi_polo" title="Sabzi polo">Sabzi polow</a> with <a href="/wiki/Fish_as_food" title="Fish as food">fish</a> (<a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iranians</a>): A traditional New Year's Day meal of rice with green herbs, served with fish. The traditional seasonings for sabzi polow are <a href="/wiki/Parsley" title="Parsley">parsley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coriander" title="Coriander">coriander</a> greens (cilantro), <a href="/wiki/Chives" title="Chives">chives</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dill" title="Dill">dill</a> herb and <a href="/wiki/Fenugreek" title="Fenugreek">fenugreek</a> greens.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Mythology">Mythology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nowruz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Mythology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nowruz_Zoroastrian.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Nowruz_Zoroastrian.jpg/220px-Nowruz_Zoroastrian.jpg" width="220" height="134" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Nowruz_Zoroastrian.jpg/330px-Nowruz_Zoroastrian.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Nowruz_Zoroastrian.jpg/440px-Nowruz_Zoroastrian.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2500" data-file-height="1523" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nowruz_Zoroastrian.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Bas-relief" class="mw-redirect" title="Bas-relief">Bas-relief</a> in Persepolis, depicting a symbol in <a href="/wiki/Zoroastrianism" title="Zoroastrianism">Zoroastrianism</a> for Nowruz.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[note 1]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>There exist various foundation myths for Nowruz in <a href="/wiki/Iranian_mythology" title="Iranian mythology">Iranian mythology</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Shahnameh" title="Shahnameh">Shahnameh</a> dates Nowruz as far back to the reign of <a href="/wiki/Jamshid" title="Jamshid">Jamshid</a>, who in <a href="/wiki/Zoroastrian" class="mw-redirect" title="Zoroastrian">Zoroastrian</a> texts saved mankind from a killer winter that was destined to kill every living creature.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[134]</a></sup> Jamshid, the mythical Iranian king, perhaps symbolizes the transition of the Proto-Iranians from animal hunting to <a href="/wiki/Animal_husbandry" title="Animal husbandry">animal husbandry</a> and a more settled life in human history.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In the Shahnameh and Iranian mythology, he is credited with the foundation of Nowruz. The book reads that Jamshid constructed a throne studded with gems. He had demons raise him above the earth into the heavens; there he sat on his throne like the sun shining in the sky. The world's creatures gathered in wonder about him and the scattered jewels around him, and called this day the <i>New Day</i> (<i>Now Ruz</i>). This was the first day of <a href="/wiki/Farvardin" title="Farvardin">Farvardin</a>, which is the first month of the <a href="/wiki/Iranian_calendar" class="mw-redirect" title="Iranian calendar">Iranian calendar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[135]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Astronomy">Astronomy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nowruz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Astronomy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/March_equinox" title="March equinox">March equinox</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Earth-lighting-equinox_EN.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Earth-lighting-equinox_EN.png/220px-Earth-lighting-equinox_EN.png" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Earth-lighting-equinox_EN.png/330px-Earth-lighting-equinox_EN.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Earth-lighting-equinox_EN.png/440px-Earth-lighting-equinox_EN.png 2x" data-file-width="1560" data-file-height="1024" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Earth-lighting-equinox_EN.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Illumination of Earth by the Sun on the day of an equinox.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The first day of the <a href="/wiki/Iranian_calendar" class="mw-redirect" title="Iranian calendar">Iranian calendar</a> falls on the <a href="/wiki/March_equinox" title="March equinox">March equinox</a>, the first day of spring, around 21 March. At the time of the equinox, the sun is observed to be directly over the <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">equator</a>, and the north and south poles of the Earth lie along the <a href="/wiki/Terminator_(solar)" title="Terminator (solar)">solar terminator</a>. Sunlight is evenly divided between the north and south <a href="/wiki/Sphere" title="Sphere">hemispheres</a>.</p>
<p>In around the 11th century CE, major reforms of the Iranian calendars took place and whose principal purpose were to fix the beginning of the calendar year, i.e. Nowruz, at the vernal equinox. Accordingly, the definition of Nowruz given by the Iranian scientist <a href="/wiki/Nasir_al-Din_al-Tusi" title="Nasir al-Din al-Tusi">Tusi</a> was the following: "the first day of the official New Year [Nowruz] was always the day on which the sun entered <a href="/wiki/Aries_(astrology)" title="Aries (astrology)">Aries</a> before noon."<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[136]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Calendar">Calendar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nowruz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Calendar">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Nowruz is the first day of <a href="/wiki/Farvardin" title="Farvardin">Farvardin</a>, the first month of the <a href="/wiki/Solar_Hijri_calendar" title="Solar Hijri calendar">Iranian solar calendar</a>.</p>
<p>In the <i>Fasli</i>/<i>Bastani</i> variant of the Zoroastrian calendar, Navroz is always the day of the <a href="/wiki/Vernal_equinox" class="mw-redirect" title="Vernal equinox">vernal equinox</a> (nominally falling on March 21).</p>
<p>In the <i>Shahenshahi</i> and <i>Kadmi</i> calendars, which do not account for leap years, the New Year's Day has drifted ahead by over 200 days. These latter two variants of the calendar, which are only followed by the Zoroastrians of Pakistan and India, celebrate the spring equinox as <i>Jamshed-i Nouroz</i>, with New Year's Day then being celebrated in JulyAugust as <a href="/wiki/Pateti" class="mw-redirect" title="Pateti">Pateti</a> "(day) of penitence" (from <i>patet</i> "confession," hence also repentance and penitence).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Nowruz_in_religions">Nowruz in religions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nowruz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Nowruz in religions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Apart from Zoroastrianism,<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[137]</a></sup> Nowruz has been entered into the contexts of some other religions and faiths.</p>
<p>There exist narrations in the <a href="/wiki/Shia_Islam" title="Shia Islam">Shia</a> literature about the merits of the day of Nowruz, including that the <a href="/wiki/The_event_of_Ghadir_Khumm" title="The event of Ghadir Khumm">Day of Ghadir</a> was on that day, and also the recommendation to fast on the day of Nowruz, the latter appearing in the fatwas of major Shia scholars.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[138]</a></sup></p>
<p>Nowruz is also a holy day for <a href="/wiki/Sufism" title="Sufism">Sufis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bektashis" class="mw-redirect" title="Bektashis">Bektashis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ismailism" class="mw-redirect" title="Ismailism">Ismailis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alawites" title="Alawites">Alawites</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-i-cias.com_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-i-cias.com-140">[139]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alevism" title="Alevism">Alevis</a>, <a href="/wiki/B%C3%A1bism" title="Bábism">Babis</a> and adherents of the <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith" title="Bahá'í Faith">Bahá'í Faith</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bahai_calendar_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bahai_calendar-141">[140]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bah.C3.A1.27.C3.AD_Faith">Bahá'í Faith</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nowruz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Bahá'í Faith">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Naw-R%C3%BAz" title="Bahá'í Naw-Rúz">Bahá'í Naw-Rúz</a></div>
<p>Naw-Rúz is one of nine holy days for adherents of the <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith" title="Bahá'í Faith">Bahá'í Faith</a> worldwide. It is the first day of the <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_calendar" title="Bahá'í calendar">Bahá'í calendar</a>, occurring on the vernal equinox around March 21.<sup id="cite_ref-walbridge_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-walbridge-142">[141]</a></sup> The Bahá'í calendar is composed of 19 months, each of 19 days,<sup id="cite_ref-bne_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bne-143">[142]</a></sup> and each of the months is named after an attribute of God; similarly each of the nineteen days in the month also are named after an attribute of God.<sup id="cite_ref-bne_143-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bne-143">[142]</a></sup> The first day and the first month were given the attribute of <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_symbols#Bah.C3.A1.E2.80.99" title="Bahá'í symbols">Bahá</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a> word meaning splendour or glory, and thus the first day of the year was the day of Bahá in the month of Bahá.<sup id="cite_ref-walbridge_142-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-walbridge-142">[141]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lehman_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lehman-144">[143]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27u%27ll%C3%A1h" title="Bahá'u'lláh">Bahá'u'lláh</a>, the founder of the Bahá'í Faith, explained that Naw-Rúz was associated with the <i>Most Great Name</i> of God,<sup id="cite_ref-walbridge_142-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-walbridge-142">[141]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lehman_144-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lehman-144">[143]</a></sup> and was instituted as a festival for those who observed the <a href="/wiki/Nineteen_day_fast" class="mw-redirect" title="Nineteen day fast">Nineteen day fast</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-prayers_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prayers-145">[144]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-aqdas_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aqdas-146">[145]</a></sup></p>
<p>The day is also used to symbolize the renewal of time in each religious dispensation.<sup id="cite_ref-iranica_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iranica-147">[146]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/%60Abdu%27l-Bah%C3%A1" title="`Abdu'l-Bahá">`Abdu'l-Bahá</a>, Bahá'u'lláh's son and successor, explained that significance of Naw-Rúz in terms of <a href="/wiki/Spring_(season)" title="Spring (season)">spring</a> and the new life it brings.<sup id="cite_ref-walbridge_142-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-walbridge-142">[141]</a></sup> He explained that the equinox is a symbol of the <a href="/wiki/Manifestation_of_God" title="Manifestation of God">messengers of God</a> and the message that they proclaim is like a spiritual springtime, and that Naw-Rúz is used to commemorate it.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[147]</a></sup></p>
<p>As with all Bahá'í holy days, there are few fixed rules for observing Naw-Rúz, and Bahá'ís all over the world celebrate it as a festive day, according to local custom.<sup id="cite_ref-walbridge_142-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-walbridge-142">[141]</a></sup> Persian Bahá'ís still observe many of the Iranian customs associated with Nowruz such as the Haft Seen, but American Bahá'í communities, for example, may have a <a href="/wiki/Potluck_dinner" class="mw-redirect" title="Potluck dinner">potluck dinner</a>, along with prayers and readings from <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_literature" title="Bahá'í literature">Bahá'í scripture</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Twelver_Shia_faith_and_Shia_Ismaili_faith">Twelver Shia faith and Shia Ismaili faith</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nowruz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Twelver Shia faith and Shia Ismaili faith">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Along with Ismailis,<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[148]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[149]</a></sup> Alawites and Alevis, the <a href="/wiki/Twelver" title="Twelver">Twelver Shia</a> also hold the day of Nowruz in high regard.</p>
<p>It has been said that <a href="/wiki/Musa_al-Kadhim" title="Musa al-Kadhim">Musa al-Kadhim</a>, the seventh <a href="/wiki/Shia" class="mw-redirect" title="Shia">Shia</a> <a href="/wiki/Imam" title="Imam">imam</a>, has explained Nowruz and said: "In Nowruz God made a covenant with His servants to worship Him and not to allow any partner for Him. To welcome, His messengers and obey their rulings. This day is the rst day that the fertile wind blow and the owers on the earth appeared. The archangel <a href="/wiki/Gabriel" title="Gabriel">Gabriel</a> appeared to the <a href="/wiki/Muhammad" title="Muhammad">Prophet</a>, and it is the day that <a href="/wiki/Abraham" title="Abraham">Abraham</a> broke the <a href="/wiki/Idolatry" title="Idolatry">idols</a>. The day Prophet Muhammad held <a href="/wiki/Ali" title="Ali">Ali</a> on his shoulders to destroy the Quraishie's idols in the house of God, the <a href="/wiki/Kaaba" title="Kaaba">Kaaba</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[150]</a></sup></p>
<p>The day upon which Nowruz falls has been recommended as a day of fasting for Twelver Shia Muslims by Shia scholars, including <a href="/wiki/Abu_al-Qasim_al-Khoei" title="Abu al-Qasim al-Khoei">Abu al-Qasim al-Khoei</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ruhollah_Khomeini" title="Ruhollah Khomeini">Ruhollah Khomeini</a><sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[151]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Ali_al-Sistani" title="Ali al-Sistani">Ali al-Sistani</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[152]</a></sup> The day also assumes special significance for Shias as it has been said that it was on 21&#160;March 656&#160;AD that the first Shia Imam, Ali, assumed the office of caliphate.</p>
